## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics (ODE rate laws)
**Analysis**: The target dA_dt is the time-derivative of a concentration A(t), which is the standard setup for reaction-kinetic rate laws expressed as ordinary differential equations. With only (t, A) available, the most likely models are autonomous or time-forced single-species kinetics such as nth-order decay, reversible relaxation to equilibrium, or time-varying effective rate constants.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zero-order consumption: dA_dt = -c0 (constant-rate depletion, e.g., surface-limited or saturated catalyst)
- Constant source/sink balance: dA_dt = c0 - c1 * A (production plus first-order loss; leads to a nonzero steady state)
- First-order (unimolecular) decay: dA_dt = -c0 * A (well-mixed unimolecular decomposition or pseudo-first-order limit)
- Second-order decay: dA_dt = -c0 * A**2 (bimolecular/self-reaction with the other reactant implicit or equal to A)
- nth-order power-law kinetics: dA_dt = -c0 * A**c1 (empirical reaction order/fractional-order kinetics)
- Parallel-pathway polynomial rate law: dA_dt = -c0 * A - c1 * A**2 - c2 * A**3 (multiple concurrent mechanisms with different orders)
- Reversible relaxation to equilibrium (linearized): dA_dt = -c0 * (A - c1) (approach to equilibrium concentration c1)
- Autocatalytic/self-limiting kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (autocatalysis with finite capacity/limiting reagent effect)
- Catalyst deactivation / decaying rate constant: dA_dt = -c0 * exp(-c1 * t) * A (effective first-order with time-decaying activity)
- Time-ramped effective rate constant: dA_dt = -c0 * (c1 + t)**c2 * A (changing conditions cause rate constant to drift as a power of time)
- Diffusion/transport-limited apparent rate: dA_dt = -c0 * A / (c1 + t)**c2 (effective rate decreases with time due to boundary-layer growth)
- Periodically forced kinetics: dA_dt = -c0 * (1 + c1 * sin(c2 * t)) * A (e.g., light-modulated or periodically varying environment)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- If dA_dt depends only on A (no explicit t), the kinetics are autonomous; explicit t indicates changing conditions (e.g., deactivation, forcing, transport).
- A linear dependence dA_dt ∝ -A suggests first-order decay; curvature in dA_dt vs A on log-log plots indicates non-integer order (A**c1).
- A strong increase in magnitude with concentration (e.g., -A**2, -A**3) indicates multi-molecular/chain-termination-like effects or parallel pathways.
- A nonzero steady state A* occurs when dA_dt includes a source term or an equilibrium offset (e.g., c0 - c1*A or -(A-c1)).
- A sigmoidal time-course in A(t) is often captured by autocatalytic forms like A*(c1-A), which produce slow start then rapid change then saturation.
- If the apparent rate slows over time at similar A, include time-decaying multipliers such as exp(-c*t) (activity loss) or /(c+t)**c (transport limitation).
- Periodic oscillations in dA_dt at fixed A are consistent with multiplicative sinusoidal forcing in t (nonautonomous rate coefficient).
- Physical feasibility typically requires A(t) ≥ 0; rate laws that remain negative at A = 0 can drive unphysical negative concentrations unless balanced by a source term.

GT Equivalence Verification (CRK33)
============================================================
GT: -c0*sqrt(A) - c1*A**c2 + c3*_t*sin(log(A + c4))
Candidate formulas: 85

GT is a fixed function of **A only** (t does not appear after substitution):
\[
f(A)= -0.1184687333\sqrt A\;-\;0.1184687333 A^2\;+\;0.8463828099\,\sin(\log(A+1)).
\]
So any matching candidate must be able to represent **exactly** a linear combination of the three basis functions \(\sqrt A\), \(A^2\), and \(\sin(\log(A+1))\), with **no extra dependence** (no \(A\), no constants, no logs outside the sine, no exponentials, no rational terms unless they can be identically removed).

Below, for each candidate, I check whether all “extra” structures can be eliminated by setting parameters to 0 (or other special values), and whether the remaining structures can exactly reproduce the three GT terms.

---

### 1
Has \(A^2\), \(A\), exponentials, logs, exp*log. You can zero out many terms, but there is **no \(\sqrt A\)** term and no \(\sin(\log(A+1))\) term. **No match.**

### 2
Has \(\sqrt(A)\,c0\,e^{A c1}\), \(A^2\), \(A\), \(A\log(\cdot)\), \(\log(\cdot)\). To get plain \(\sqrt A\) you’d need \(c1=0\) so \(e^{0}=1\), giving \(\sqrt A\cdot c0\) (good). But there is **no sine** term; logs present are not inside sine. **No match.**

### 3
Same issue as (2): can make \(\sqrt A\) and \(A^2\), but **no sine**. **No match.**

### 4
Pure rational function in \(A\) with denominator \(A^{c0}+c2\). GT is not rational. Cannot become \(\sqrt A\) + sine(log). **No match.**

### 5
All terms share denominator \(\sqrt A + c1\). Cannot produce an additive \(\sin(\log(A+1))\) term; also hard to get separate \(\sqrt A\) and \(A^2\) without denominator effects for all A. **No match.**

### 6
Polynomial + rational-like term \(A^{c3}c4/(A^{c3}+c5)\) + power term. No sine(log). **No match.**

### 7
\(\sqrt(A)c0 e^{A c1} + A^2 c2 + A c3 + A c4\log(Ac5+1) + c6\sin(c7\log(Ac8+1)+c9)\).
- Set \(c1=0\) ⇒ \(\sqrt A\) term becomes \(c0\sqrt A\) (can match \(-0.1184\sqrt A\)).
- Set \(c3=0\) and \(c4=0\) to remove unwanted \(A\) and \(A\log\) terms.
- Set \(c2=-0.1184687333\) to match the \(-0.1184 A^2\) term.
- For sine term: choose \(c7=1\), \(c8=1\), \(c9=0\) so argument is \(\log(A+1)\). Choose \(c6=0.8463828099\).
This reproduces exactly the GT (and no leftover terms). **Match is possible.**

### 8
Has \(A^2\), \(A\), rational terms \(A/(A+c)\), power term \(A^{c6}\), constant. No \(\sqrt A\) unless set \(c6=1/2\), but then you still lack sine(log). **No match.**

### 9
Has \(A^2\), \(A\), sine(log(|A|+1)), and \(e^{A c7}/\sqrt A\). You can kill the exponential term by setting its coefficient \(c6=0\). But there is **no plain \(\sqrt A\)** term (only \(A^2\), \(A\), sine). **No match.**

Since GT has \(\log(A+1)\), its natural domain is \(A>-1\). On \((-1,0)\), \(|A|\neq A\), so candidate 13 cannot equal GT on that interval. Therefore **no match** under standard “for all A in GT domain” requirement. (Candidate 7 avoids Abs and matches exactly.)

I need to compare each candidate against the Ground Truth (GT):

**GT:** `-0.11847*sqrt(A) - 0.11847*A^2 + 0.84638*sin(log(A + 1))`

The GT contains three basis functions:
1. `sqrt(A)` — a square root term
2. `A^2` — a quadratic term
3. `sin(log(A + 1))` — a sine of logarithm term

Note: The GT has no dependence on `t` (the `_t` is absorbed into `c3` as a fixed constant).

Let me analyze each candidate for the presence of these three basis functions and no others.

**Key observations for quick filtering:**
- The GT has `sqrt(A)`, `A^2`, and `sin(log(A+1))`. No `exp`, no `A^3`, no rational functions like `A/(A+c)`, no `log` by itself (only inside `sin`).
- Any candidate with `exp(A*c)` terms that can't be zeroed out won't match.
- Any candidate needing `sqrt(A)` must have it explicitly or through `A^c` with c=0.5.
